<p><b>George Roger Waters</b> (born 6 September 1943) is an English musician, singer, songwriter, multi-instrumentalist, and composer. In 1965, he co-founded the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> with drummer <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Nick Mason</a>, keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a> and guitarist, singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Syd_Barrett" title="Syd Barrett">Syd Barrett</a>. Waters initially served as the group's bassist and co-lead vocalist, but following the departure of Barrett in 1968, he also became their lyricist and conceptual leader.</p>
<p>Pink Floyd subsequently achieved international success with the <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept albums</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="The Dark Side of the Moon">The Dark Side of the Moon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd album)">Wish You Were Here</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Animals_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Animals (Pink Floyd album)">Animals</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Cut_(album)" title="The Final Cut (album)">The Final Cut</a></i>. By the early 1980s, they had become one of the most critically acclaimed and best-selling acts in the history of popular music; as of 2013, they have sold more than 250 million albums worldwide, including 74.5 million units sold in the United States. Amid creative differences within the group, Waters left in 1985 and began a legal dispute with the remaining members over their intended use of the band's name and material. They settled out of court in 1987, and nearly eighteen years passed before he performed with them again.</p>
<p>Waters' solo career has included three studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking" title="The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking">The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_K.A.O.S." title="Radio K.A.O.S.">Radio K.A.O.S.</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Amused_to_Death" title="Amused to Death">Amused to Death</a></i>. In 1990, he staged one of the largest and most extravagant rock concerts in history, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_%E2%80%93_Live_in_Berlin" title="The Wall – Live in Berlin">The Wall – Live in Berlin</a></i>, with an official attendance of 200,000. As a member of Pink Floyd, he was inducted into the US <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1996 and the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> in 2005. That same year he released <i><span lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/%C3%87a_Ira_(opera)" title="Ça Ira (opera)">Ça Ira</a></span></i>, an <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> in three acts translated from <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Roda-Gil" title="Étienne Roda-Gil">Étienne</a> and Nadine Roda-Gils' <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">libretto</a> about the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. Later that year, he reunited with Pink Floyd bandmates Mason, Wright and <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> global awareness event; it was the group's first appearance with Waters since 1981. He has toured extensively as a solo act since 1999 and played <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> in its entirety for his <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon_Live" title="The Dark Side of the Moon Live">world tour of 2006–2008</a>. In 2010, he began <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Live_(concert_tour)" title="The Wall Live (concert tour)">The Wall Live</a> and in 2011 Gilmour and Mason appeared with him during a performance of the double album in London. As of 2013, the tour is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">highest-grossing of all time by a solo artist</a>.</p>
<p>Waters has been married four times; first in 1969 to his childhood sweetheart <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judy_Trim" title="Judy Trim">Judy Trim</a>; they had no children together and divorced in 1975. The following year he married <a href="/wiki/Carolyne_Christie" title="Carolyne Christie">Lady Carolyne Christie</a>; the marriage produced a son, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Waters" title="Harry Waters">Harry Waters</a>, a musician who has played keyboards with his father's touring band since 2006, and a daughter, India Waters, who has worked as a model. Christie and Waters divorced in 1992, and in 1993, he married Priscilla Phillips. They had one son together, Jack Fletcher, before getting divorced in 2001. In 2012, Waters married actress and filmmaker Laurie Durning.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1943.E2.80.931964:_early_years">1943–1964: early years</span></h2>
<p>George Roger Waters was born on 6 September 1943, the younger of two boys, to Mary (née Whyte; 1913-2009) and Eric Fletcher Waters (1913-1944), in <a href="/wiki/Great_Bookham" title="Great Bookham">Great Bookham</a>, Surrey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson20137_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson20137-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> His father, the son of a coal miner and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> activist, was a schoolteacher, a devout Christian, and a <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Great_Britain" title="Communist Party of Great Britain">Communist Party</a> member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200813_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200813-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In the early years of the Second World War, his father was a <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objector</a> who drove an ambulance during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200813_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200813-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He later changed his stance on pacifism and joined the British Army, and as a 2Lt. of the 8th <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fusiliers" title="Royal Fusiliers">Royal Fusiliers</a> died at <a href="/wiki/Aprilia,_Lazio" title="Aprilia, Lazio">Aprilia</a>, between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Shingle" title="Operation Shingle">Anzio</a> and Rome in Italy, on 18 February 1944, when Roger was five months old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> On 19 February 2014, Waters unveiled a monument to his father and other war casualties there, and was made an honorary citizen of Anzio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Following her husband's death, Mary Waters, also a teacher, moved with her two sons to <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a> and raised them there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManning20065.E2.80.936_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManning20065.E2.80.936-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Roger Waters' earliest memory is of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VJ_Day" title="VJ Day">VJ Day</a> celebrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DID_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-DID-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Mary Waters died in 2009, aged 96.</p>
<p>Waters attended Morley Memorial Junior School in Cambridge and then the <a href="/wiki/Cambridgeshire_High_School_for_Boys" title="Cambridgeshire High School for Boys">Cambridgeshire High School for Boys</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Hills_Road_Sixth_Form_College" title="Hills Road Sixth Form College">Hills Road Sixth Form College</a>) with <a href="/wiki/Syd_Barrett" title="Syd Barrett">Syd Barrett</a>, while his future musical partner, <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>, lived nearby on the city's Mill Road, and attended <a href="/wiki/The_Perse_School" title="The Perse School">the Perse School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatkinsonAnderson199115.E2.80.9318_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatkinsonAnderson199115.E2.80.9318-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> At 15, Waters was chairman of the Cambridge <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Nuclear_Disarmament" title="Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament">Youth Campaign for Nuclear Disarmament</a> (YCND),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200512.E2.80.9313_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200512.E2.80.9313-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> having designed its publicity poster and participated in its organisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey200813_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey200813-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Though he was a keen sportsman and a highly regarded member of the high school's cricket and rugby teams,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatkinsonAnderson199123_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatkinsonAnderson199123-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> he disliked his educational experience; according to Waters, "I hated every second of it, apart from games. The regime at school was a very oppressive one ... the same kids who are susceptible to bullying by other kids are also susceptible to bullying by the teachers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200814.E2.80.9319_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200814.E2.80.9319-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Whereas Waters knew Barrett and Gilmour from his childhood in Cambridge, he met future Pink Floyd founder members <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Nick Mason</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a> in London at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Westminster" title="University of Westminster">Regent Street Polytechnic</a> (later the University of Westminster) school of architecture. Waters enrolled there in 1962, after a series of aptitude tests indicated he was well-suited to that field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008320_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008320-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> He had initially considered a career in mechanical engineering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200836_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200836-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1965.E2.80.931985:_Pink_Floyd">1965–1985: Pink Floyd</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_and_Barrett-led_period">Formation and Barrett-led period</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg"><img alt="A monochrome image of Roger Waters playing bass guitar. He has shoulder-length hair, black attire, and is standing in front of a microphone." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="265" data-file-width="194" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg/170px-Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roger_waters_leeds_1970.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Waters performing with Pink Floyd at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_University" title="Leeds University">Leeds University</a> in 1970</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By September 1963, Waters and Mason had lost interest in their studies; they had moved into the lower flat of Stanhope Gardens, owned by Mike Leonard, a part-time tutor at the Regent Street Polytechnic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters, Mason and Wright first played music together in the autumn of 1963, in a band formed by vocalist Keith Noble and bassist Clive Metcalfe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> They usually called themselves Sigma 6, but also used the name the Meggadeaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey200813_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey200813-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters played rhythm guitar and Mason played drums, Wright played on any keyboard he could arrange to use, and Noble's sister Sheilagh provided an occasional vocal accompaniment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200517.E2.80.9318_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200517.E2.80.9318-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In the early years the band performed during private functions and rehearsed in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tearoom" title="Tearoom">tearoom</a> in the basement of Regent Street Polytechnic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200513.E2.80.9318_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200513.E2.80.9318-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When Metcalfe and Noble left to form their own group in September 1963, the remaining members asked Barrett and guitar player <a href="/wiki/Bob_Klose" title="Bob Klose">Bob Klose</a> to join.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> By January 1964, the group became known as the Abdabs, or the Screaming Abdabs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey200814_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey200814-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> During the autumn of 1964, the band used the names Leonard's Lodgers, Spectrum Five, and eventually, the Tea Set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey200818.2C_28_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey200818.2C_28-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Sometime during the autumn of 1965, the Tea Set began calling itself the Pink Floyd Sound, later the Pink Floyd and by early 1966, Pink Floyd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By early 1966 Barrett was Pink Floyd's front-man, guitarist, and songwriter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200587_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200587-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote or co-wrote all but one track of their debut LP <i><a href="/wiki/The_Piper_at_the_Gates_of_Dawn" title="The Piper at the Gates of Dawn">The Piper at the Gates of Dawn</a></i>, released in August 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200587.E2.80.93107_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200587.E2.80.93107-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters contributed the song "<a href="/wiki/Take_Up_Thy_Stethoscope_and_Walk" title="Take Up Thy Stethoscope and Walk">Take Up Thy Stethoscope and Walk</a>" (his first sole writing credit) to the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200891_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200891-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> By late 1967, Barrett's deteriorating mental health and increasingly erratic behaviour,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake200890.E2.80.93114_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake200890.E2.80.93114-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> rendered him "unable or unwilling"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005129_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005129-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> to continue in his capacity as Pink Floyd's singer-songwriter and lead guitarist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason200587.E2.80.93107_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason200587.E2.80.93107-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In early March 1968 Pink Floyd met with managers <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jenner" title="Peter Jenner">Peter Jenner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_King_(music_manager)" title="Andrew King (music manager)">Andrew King</a> of <a href="/wiki/Blackhill_Enterprises" title="Blackhill Enterprises">Blackhill Enterprises</a> to discuss the band's future. Barrett agreed to leave Pink Floyd, and the band "agreed to Blackhill's entitlement in perpetuity" regarding "past activities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005105_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005105-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The band's new manager <a href="/wiki/Steve_O%27Rourke" title="Steve O'Rourke">Steve O'Rourke</a> made a formal announcement about the departure of Barrett and the arrival of David Gilmour in April 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005106_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005106-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waters-led_period">Waters-led period</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg"><img alt="A monochrome image of Pink Floyd performing on a concert stage. Each band member is illuminated from above by bright spotlights" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1000" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg/220px-DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg/330px-DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg/440px-DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DarkSideOfTheMoon1973.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A live performance of <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> at <a href="/wiki/Earls_Court" title="Earls Court">Earls Court</a>, shortly after its release in 1973: (l-r) David Gilmour, Nick Mason, <a href="/wiki/Dick_Parry" title="Dick Parry">Dick Parry</a>, Roger Waters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Filling the void left by Barrett's departure in March 1968, Waters began to chart Pink Floyd's artistic direction. He became the principal songwriter, lyricist and co-lead vocalist (along with Gilmour, and at times, Wright), and would remain the band's dominant creative figure until his departure in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005106.E2.80.93107.2C_160.E2.80.93161.2C_265.2C_278_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005106.E2.80.93107.2C_160.E2.80.93161.2C_265.2C_278-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote the lyrics to the five Pink Floyd albums preceding his own departure, starting with <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> (1973) and ending with <i>The Final Cut</i> (1983), while exerting progressively more creative control over the band and its music. Every Waters studio album since <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="The Dark Side of the Moon">The Dark Side of the Moon</a></i> has been a <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake20083.2C_9.2C_113.2C_156.2C_242.2C_279.2C_320.2C_398_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake20083.2C_9.2C_113.2C_156.2C_242.2C_279.2C_320.2C_398-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> With lyrics written entirely by Waters, <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> was one of the most commercially successful rock albums ever. It spent 736 straight weeks on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 chart—until July 1988—and sold over 40 million copies worldwide. It was continuing to sell over 8,000 units every week as of 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Pink Floyd biographer Glen Povey, <i>Dark Side</i> is the world's second best-selling album, and the United States' 21st best-selling album of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008345_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008345-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Waters produced thematic ideas that became the impetus for the Pink Floyd concept albums <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> (1973), <i><a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd album)">Wish You Were Here</a></i> (1975), <i><a href="/wiki/Animals_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Animals (Pink Floyd album)">Animals</a></i> (1977) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i> (1979)—written largely by Waters—and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Cut_(album)" title="The Final Cut (album)">The Final Cut</a></i> (1983)—written entirely by Waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005265.E2.80.93269_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005265.E2.80.93269-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> He referred or alluded to the cost of war and the loss of his father throughout his work, from "<a href="/wiki/Corporal_Clegg" title="Corporal Clegg">Corporal Clegg</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/A_Saucerful_of_Secrets" title="A Saucerful of Secrets">A Saucerful of Secrets</a></i>, 1968) and "<a href="/wiki/Free_Four" title="Free Four">Free Four</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Obscured_by_Clouds" title="Obscured by Clouds">Obscured by Clouds</a></i>, 1972) to "<a href="/wiki/Us_and_Them_(song)" title="Us and Them (song)">Us and Them</a>" from <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i>, "<a href="/wiki/When_the_Tigers_Broke_Free" title="When the Tigers Broke Free">When the Tigers Broke Free</a>", first used in the feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd_%E2%80%93_The_Wall" title="Pink Floyd – The Wall">The Wall</a></i> (1982), later included with "<a href="/wiki/The_Fletcher_Memorial_Home" title="The Fletcher Memorial Home">The Fletcher Memorial Home</a>" on <i>The Final Cut</i>, an album dedicated to his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The theme and composition of <i>The Wall</i> was influenced by his upbringing in an English society depleted of men after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294.E2.80.93295.2C_351_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294.E2.80.93295.2C_351-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #FFFFF0;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>I think things like "Comfortably Numb" were the last embers of mine and Roger's ability to work collaboratively together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008275_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008275-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: center;">—<a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a></div>
</div>
<p>The double album <i>The Wall</i> was written almost entirely by Waters and is largely based on his life story,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008260_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008260-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> and having sold over 23 million <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">RIAA certified units</a> in the US as of 2013, is one of the top three best-selling albums of all time in America, according to RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Pink Floyd hired <a href="/wiki/Bob_Ezrin" title="Bob Ezrin">Bob Ezrin</a> to co-produce the album, and cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Scarfe" title="Gerald Scarfe">Gerald Scarfe</a> to illustrate the album's sleeve art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008260.E2.80.93261_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008260.E2.80.93261-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The band embarked on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wall_Tour" title="The Wall Tour">The Wall Tour</a> of Los Angeles, New York, London, and Dortmund. The last band performance of <i>The Wall</i> was on 16 June 1981, at Earls Court London, and this was Pink Floyd's last appearance with Waters until the band's brief reunion at 2 July 2005 Live 8 concert in London's Hyde Park, 24 years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPoveyRussell1997185_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPoveyRussell1997185-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1983, the last Waters–Gilmour–Mason collaboration, <i>The Final Cut</i>, was released. The album was subtitled: "A requiem for the post-war dream by Roger Waters, performed by Pink Floyd".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008230_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008230-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters wrote all the album's lyrics as well as the music. His lyrics were critical of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> government of the day and mention Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> by name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294.E2.80.93299_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008294.E2.80.93299-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> At the time Gilmour did not have any new material, so he asked Waters to delay the recording until he could write some songs, but Waters refused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008295_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008295-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Mason, after power struggles within the band and creative arguments about the album, Gilmour's name "disappeared" from the production credits, though he retained his pay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005264.E2.80.93270_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005264.E2.80.93270-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine gave the album five stars, with <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Loder" title="Kurt Loder">Kurt Loder</a> describing it as "a superlative achievement" and "art rock's crowning masterpiece".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Loder viewed the work as "essentially a Roger Waters solo album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Amidst creative differences within the group, Waters left Pink Floyd in 1985, and began a legal battle with the remaining band members regarding their continued use of the name and material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008240.E2.80.93241_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008240.E2.80.93241-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1985, Waters "issued a statement to EMI and CBS invoking the 'Leaving Member' clause" on his contract. In October 1986, he initiated <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> proceedings to formally dissolve the Pink Floyd partnership. In his submission to the High Court he called Pink Floyd a "spent force creatively".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008221.2C_237.2C_240.E2.80.93241.2C_246_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008221.2C_237.2C_240.E2.80.93241.2C_246-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Gilmour and Mason opposed the application and announced their intention to continue as Pink Floyd. Waters claims to have been forced to resign much like Wright some years earlier, and he decided to leave Pink Floyd based on legal considerations, stating " ... because, if I hadn't, the financial repercussions would have wiped me out completely."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008312.E2.80.93313_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008312.E2.80.93313-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1987, an agreement between Waters and Pink Floyd was reached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008240.E2.80.93241_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008240.E2.80.93241-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Mason:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We eventually formalised a settlement with Roger. On Christmas Eve, 1987, ... David and Roger convened for a summit meeting on the houseboat [the <i><a href="/wiki/Astoria_(recording_studio)" title="Astoria (recording studio)">Astoria</a></i>] with Jerome Walton, David's accountant. Jerome painstakingly typed out the bones of a settlement. Essentially—although there was far more complex detail—the arrangement allowed Roger to be freed from his arrangement with Steve [O'Rourke], and David and me to continue working under the name <i>Pink Floyd</i>. In the end the court accepted Jerome's version as the final and binding document and duly stamped it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005293.E2.80.93294_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005293.E2.80.93294-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Waters was released from his contractual obligation with O'Rourke, and he retained the copyrights to <i>The Wall</i> concept and his trademarked inflatable pig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManning2006139_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManning2006139-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The Gilmour-led Pink Floyd released three studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/A_Momentary_Lapse_of_Reason" title="A Momentary Lapse of Reason">A Momentary Lapse of Reason</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">The Division Bell</a></i> (1994) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Endless_River" title="The Endless River">The Endless River</a></i> (2014). As of 2013, it is estimated that Pink Floyd have sold over 250 million albums worldwide, including 74.5 million RIAA certified units sold in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1984.E2.80.93present:_solo_career">1984–present: solo career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1984.E2.80.931996">1984–1996</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-405,_Berlin,_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg"><img alt="A wall covered in graffiti with a circular movie screen and lights atop it. </div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401,_Berlin,_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg"><img alt="A concert stage in front of a wall with 2 levels.
