On the lower level is a drum kit and a man playing guitar." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="726" data-file-width="519" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401%2C_Berlin%2C_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0722-401,_Berlin,_Auff%C3%BChrung_der_Rockoper_%22The_Wall%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Wall – Live in Berlin</i>, 21 July 1990</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the release of <i>The Final Cut</i>, Waters embarked on a solo career that produced three concept albums and a movie soundtrack. In 1984, he released his first solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking" title="The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking">The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking</a></i>, a project about a man's dreams across one night that dealt with Waters' feelings about monogamy and family life versus "the call of the wild".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> In the end the character, Reg, chooses love and matrimony over promiscuity. The album featured guitarist <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, jazz saxophonist <a href="/wiki/David_Sanborn" title="David Sanborn">David Sanborn</a>, and artwork by Gerald Scarfe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Kurt Loder described <i>The Pros And Cons of Hitch Hiking</i> as a "strangely static, faintly hideous record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008305.E2.80.93306_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008305.E2.80.93306-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> rated the album a "rock bottom" one star."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991272.E2.80.93273-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Years later, Mike DeGagne of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> praised the album for its, "ingenious symbolism" and "brilliant use of stream of consciousness within a subconscious realm", rating it four out of five stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters began touring in support of the new album, aided by Clapton, a new band, new material, and a selection of Pink Floyd favourites. Waters débuted <a href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking_(tour)" title="The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking (tour)">his tour</a> in Stockholm on 16 June 1984. Poor ticket sales plagued the tour, and some of the larger venues had to be cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008332.E2.80.93333_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008332.E2.80.93333-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> By his own estimate, he lost £400,000 on the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008309_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008309-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1985, Waters went to North America to play smaller venues with the Pros and Cons Plus Some Old Pink Floyd Stuff — North America Tour 1985. <i>The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking</i> has been certified Gold by the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAGPC_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAGPC-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1986, Waters contributed songs and a score to the soundtrack of the animated movie <i><a href="/wiki/When_the_Wind_Blows_(1986_film)" title="When the Wind Blows (1986 film)">When the Wind Blows</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Briggs" title="Raymond Briggs">Raymond Briggs</a> <a href="/wiki/When_the_Wind_Blows_(comics)" title="When the Wind Blows (comics)">book of the same name</a>. His backing band featuring <a href="/wiki/Paul_Carrack" title="Paul Carrack">Paul Carrack</a> was credited as <i>The Bleeding Heart Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch200536_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch200536-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1987, Waters released <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_K.A.O.S." title="Radio K.A.O.S.">Radio K.A.O.S.</a></i>, a concept album based on a mute man named Billy from an impoverished Welsh mining town who has the ability to physically tune into radio waves in his head. Billy first learns to communicate with a radio DJ, and eventually to control the world's computers. Angry at the state of the world in which he lives, he simulates a nuclear attack. Waters followed the release with a supporting tour also in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManning2006131_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManning2006131-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> fell, and in July 1990 Waters staged one of the largest and most elaborate rock concerts in history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPoveyRussell1997246.E2.80.93247_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPoveyRussell1997246.E2.80.93247-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_%E2%80%93_Live_in_Berlin" title="The Wall – Live in Berlin">The Wall – Live in Berlin</a></i>, on the vacant terrain between <a href="/wiki/Potsdamer_Platz" title="Potsdamer Platz">Potsdamer Platz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>. The show reported an official attendance of 200,000, though some estimates are as much as twice that, with approximately one billion television viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008346_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008346-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cheshire" title="Leonard Cheshire">Leonard Cheshire</a> asked him to do the concert to raise funds for charity. Waters' group of musicians included <a href="/wiki/Joni_Mitchell" title="Joni Mitchell">Joni Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Morrison" title="Van Morrison">Van Morrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)" title="Scorpions (band)">Scorpions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sin%C3%A9ad_O%27Connor" title="Sinéad O'Connor">Sinéad O'Connor</a>. Waters also used an East German symphony orchestra and choir, a <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> marching band, and a pair of helicopters from the US <a href="/wiki/7th_Airborne_Command_and_Control_Squadron" title="7th Airborne Command and Control Squadron">7th Airborne Command and Control Squadron</a>. Designed by Mark Fisher, the Wall was 25 metres tall and 170 metres long and was built across the set. Scarfe's inflatable puppets were recreated on an enlarged scale, and although many rock icons received invitations to the show, Gilmour, Mason, and Wright, did not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008342.E2.80.93347_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008342.E2.80.93347-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters released a concert double album of the performance which has been certified platinum by the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAGPC_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAGPC-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, Waters hired manager Mark Fenwick and left EMI for a worldwide deal with Columbia. He released his third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Amused_to_Death" title="Amused to Death">Amused to Death</a></i>, in 1992. The record is heavily influenced by the events of the <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square_protests_of_1989" title="Tiananmen Square protests of 1989">Tiananmen Square protests of 1989</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, and a critique of the notion of war becoming the subject of entertainment, particularly on television. The title was derived from the book <i><a href="/wiki/Amusing_Ourselves_to_Death" title="Amusing Ourselves to Death">Amusing Ourselves to Death</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Neil_Postman" title="Neil Postman">Neil Postman</a>. <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Leonard" title="Patrick Leonard">Patrick Leonard</a>, who worked on <i>A Momentary Lapse of Reason</i>, co-produced the album. <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> played lead guitar on many of the album's tracks, which were recorded with an impressive cast of musicians at ten different recording studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008348.E2.80.93349_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008348.E2.80.93349-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> It is Waters' most critically acclaimed solo recording, garnering some comparison to his previous work with Pink Floyd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008347.E2.80.93352_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008347.E2.80.93352-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters described the record as, a "stunning piece of work", ranking the album with <i>Dark Side of the Moon</i> and <i>The Wall</i> as one of the best of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManning2006141.2C_252_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManning2006141.2C_252-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The album had one hit, the song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/What_God_Wants" title="What God Wants">What God Wants</a>, Pt. 1", which reached number 35 in the UK in September 1992 and number 5 on <i>Billboard</i> '​s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Mainstream_Rock_Tracks" title="Hot Mainstream Rock Tracks">Mainstream Rock Tracks</a> chart in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RWAM_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-RWAM-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Amused to Death</i> was certified Silver by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales of <i>Amused to Death</i> topped out at around one million and there was no tour in support of the album. Waters would first perform material from it seven years later during his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_the_Flesh_(tour)" title="In the Flesh (tour)">In the Flesh tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008323.E2.80.93324_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008323.E2.80.93324-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1996, Waters was inducted into the US and UK <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Halls of Fame</a> as a member of Pink Floyd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932004">1999–2004</span></h3>
<p>In 1999, after a 12-year hiatus from touring, and a seven-year absence from the music industry, Waters embarked on the In the Flesh tour, performing both solo and Pink Floyd material. The tour was a financial success in the US and though Waters had booked mostly smaller venues, tickets sold so well that many of the concerts were upgraded to larger ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008329.E2.80.93334_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008329.E2.80.93334-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour eventually stretched across the world and would span three years. A concert film was released on CD and DVD, named <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Flesh_%E2%80%93_Live" title="In the Flesh – Live">In the Flesh – Live</a></i>. During the tour, he played two new songs "Flickering Flame" and "Each Small Candle" as the final encore to many of the shows. In June 2002, he completed the tour with a performance in front of 70,000 people at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival of Performing Arts</a>, playing 15 Pink Floyd songs and five songs from his solo catalogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008329.E2.80.93334_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008329.E2.80.93334-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Miramax" title="Miramax">Miramax</a> announced in mid-2004 that a production of <i>The Wall</i> was to appear on Broadway with Waters playing a prominent role in the creative direction. Reports stated that the musical contained not only the original tracks from <i>The Wall</i>, but also songs from <i>Dark Side of the Moon</i>, <i>Wish You Were Here</i> and other Pink Floyd albums, as well as new material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> On the night of 1 May 2004, recorded extracts from the opera, including its <a href="/wiki/Overture" title="Overture">overture</a>, were played on the occasion of the <i><a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">Welcome Europe</a></i> celebrations in the accession country of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>. Gert Hof mixed recorded excerpts from the opera into a continuous piece of music which was played as an accompaniment to a large light and fireworks display over <a href="/wiki/Grand_Harbour" title="Grand Harbour">Grand Harbour</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008334_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008334-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 2004, Waters released two new tracks on the Internet: "To Kill the Child", inspired by the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, and "Leaving Beirut", an anti-war song "inspired by his travels in the Middle East as a teenager".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.93present">2005–present</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg"><img alt="A concert stage lit by purple lighting. Four men are performing on the stage as a crowd stands in front of it. Behind the men are video screens displaying images of vinyl records." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg/220px-Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg/330px-Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg/440px-Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pink_floyd_live_8_london.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Waters (far right) performing with Pink Floyd at Live 8, 2 July 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RogerWaters03.jpg"><img alt="Roger Waters, dressed in black, playing a bass guitar and speaking into a microphone. Behind him are several red vertical video panels." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="835" data-file-width="631" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/RogerWaters03.jpg/170px-RogerWaters03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/RogerWaters03.jpg/255px-RogerWaters03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/RogerWaters03.jpg/340px-RogerWaters03.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RogerWaters03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Waters playing "In the Flesh" on his Dark Side of the Moon Tour at Viking Stadion, Stavanger, 26 June 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2005, Waters reunited with Mason, Wright, and Gilmour for what would be their final performance together at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> concert in London's Hyde Park, Pink Floyd's only appearance with Waters since their final performance of <i>The Wall</i> at Earls Court London 24 years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008237.2C_266.E2.80.93267_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008237.2C_266.E2.80.93267-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> They played a 23-minute set consisting of "<a href="/wiki/Speak_to_Me" title="Speak to Me">Speak to Me</a>/<a href="/wiki/Breathe_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Breathe (Pink Floyd song)">Breathe</a>"/"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathe_(Reprise)" title="Breathe (Reprise)">Breathe (Reprise)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Money_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Money (Pink Floyd song)">Money</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd song)">Wish You Were Here</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Comfortably_Numb" title="Comfortably Numb">Comfortably Numb</a>". Waters told the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> that while the experience of playing with Pink Floyd again was positive, the chances of a bona fide reunion would be "slight" considering his and Gilmour's continuing musical and ideological differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991308_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1991308-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Though Waters had differing ideas about which songs they should play, he "agreed to roll over for one night only",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008382.E2.80.93383_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008382.E2.80.93383-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Gilmour told the Associated Press, "The rehearsals convinced me it wasn't something I wanted to be doing a lot of. There have been all sorts of farewell moments in people's lives and careers which they have then rescinded, but I think I can fairly categorically say that there won't be a tour or an album again that I take part in. It isn't to do with animosity or anything like that. It's just that ... I've been there, I've done it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2005, Pink Floyd were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2005, Waters released <i><span lang="fr">Ça Ira</span></i> (pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[sa iˈʁa]</a></span>, French for "it will be fine"; Waters added the subtitle, "There is Hope"), an opera in three acts translated from the late <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Roda-Gil" title="Étienne Roda-Gil">Étienne Roda-Gil</a>'s French libretto based on the historical subject of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><span lang="fr">Ça Ira</span></i> was released as a double CD album, featuring baritone <a href="/wiki/Bryn_Terfel" title="Bryn Terfel">Bryn Terfel</a>, soprano <a href="/wiki/Ying_Huang" title="Ying Huang">Ying Huang</a> and tenor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Groves_(tenor)" title="Paul Groves (tenor)">Paul Groves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008324.E2.80.93325_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008324.E2.80.93325-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Set during the early French Revolution, the original libretto was co-written in French by Roda-Gil and his wife Nadine Delahaye. Waters had begun rewriting the libretto in English in 1989,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManning2006256_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManning2006256-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> and said about the composition: "I've always been a big fan of Beethoven's choral music, <a href="/wiki/Hector_Berlioz" title="Hector Berlioz">Berlioz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Borodin" title="Alexander Borodin">Borodin</a> ... This is unashamedly romantic and resides in that early 19th-century tradition, because that's where my tastes lie in classical and choral music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008392_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008392-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters appeared on television to discuss the opera, but the interviews often focused instead on his relationship with Pink Floyd, something Waters would "take in stride", a sign Pink Floyd biographer <a href="/wiki/Mark_Blake_(writer)" title="Mark Blake (writer)">Mark Blake</a> believes to be, "a testament to his mellower old age or twenty years of dedicated psychotherapy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008392_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008392-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><span lang="fr">Ça Ira</span></i> reached number 5 on the <i>Billboard</i> Classical Music Chart in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2006, Waters commenced <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon_Live" title="The Dark Side of the Moon Live">The Dark Side of the Moon Live</a> tour, a two-year, world-spanning effort that began in Europe in June and North America in September. The first half of the show featured both Pink Floyd songs and Waters' solo material, while the second half included a complete live performance of the 1973 Pink Floyd album <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i>, the first time in over three decades that Waters had performed the album. The shows ended with an encore from the third side of <i>The Wall</i>. He utilised elaborate staging by concert lighting designer <a href="/wiki/Marc_Brickman" title="Marc Brickman">Marc Brickman</a> complete with laser lights, fog machines, pyrotechnics, psychedelic projections, and inflatable floating puppets (Spaceman and Pig) controlled by a "handler" dressed as a butcher, and a full 360-degree <a href="/wiki/Quadraphonic_sound" title="Quadraphonic sound">quadraphonic sound</a> system was used. Nick Mason joined Waters for <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> set and the encores on select 2006 tour dates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey2008319.2C_334.E2.80.93338_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey2008319.2C_334.E2.80.93338-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters continued touring in January 2007 in Australia and New Zealand, then Asia, Europe, South America, and back to North America in June.</p>
<p>In March 2007, the Waters song, "Hello (I Love You)" was featured in the science fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Mimzy" title="The Last Mimzy">The Last Mimzy</a></i>. The song plays over the film's end credits. He released it as a single, on CD and via download, and described it as, "a song that captures the themes of the movie, the clash between humanity's best and worst instincts, and how a child's innocence can win the day".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> He performed at California's <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Festival</a> in April 2008 and was to be among the headlining artists performing at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_Earth_India_2008#Live_Earth_India_2008" title="Live Earth India 2008">Live Earth 2008</a> in Mumbai, India in December 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> but that concert was cancelled in light of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Mumbai_attacks" title="2008 Mumbai attacks">26 November terrorist attacks</a> in Mumbai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_(The_Wall_Live)_-_01.jpg"><img alt="Waters on stage wearing sunglasses and a black leather coat. He is holding a microphone up to his mouth." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1716" data-file-width="2145" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg/220px-Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg/330px-Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg/440px-Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_%28The_Wall_Live%29_-_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Waters_en_el_Palau_Sant_Jordi_de_Barcelona_(The_Wall_Live)_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roger Waters in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, during <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Live_(concert_tour)" title="The Wall Live (concert tour)">The Wall Live</a> in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Waters confirmed the possibility of an upcoming solo album which "might be called" <i>Heartland</i>, and has said he has numerous songs written (some already recorded) that he intends to release when they are a complete album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2010, Waters released a cover of "<a href="/wiki/We_Shall_Overcome" title="We Shall Overcome">We Shall Overcome</a>", a protest song rewritten and arranged by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Carawan" title="Guy Carawan">Guy Carawan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">Pete Seeger</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highlander_Folk_School" title="Highlander Folk School">Highlander Folk School</a> possibly derived either from the refrain of a gospel hymn published by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Albert_Tindley" title="Charles Albert Tindley">Charles Albert Tindley</a> in 1901, but more likely from <a href="/wiki/Louise_Shropshire" title="Louise Shropshire">Louise Shropshire</a>'s hymn, "If My Jesus Wills." He performed with David Gilmour at the Hoping Foundation Benefit Evening in July 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The four-song set included: "<a href="/wiki/To_Know_Him_Is_to_Love_Him" title="To Know Him Is to Love Him">To Know Him Is to Love Him</a>", which was played in early Pink Floyd sound checks, followed by "Wish You Were Here", "Comfortably Numb", and "Another Brick in the Wall (Part Two)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2010, Waters commenced <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Live_(concert_tour)" title="The Wall Live (concert tour)">The Wall Live</a> tour, an updated version of the original Pink Floyd shows, featuring a complete performance of <i>The Wall</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Cole Moreton of the <i>Daily Mail</i>, "The touring version of Pink Floyd's <i>The Wall</i> is one of the most ambitious and complex rock shows ever ...",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CMDM_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-CMDM-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and it is estimated that the tour cost £37 million to stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CMDM_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-CMDM-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters told the Associated Press that The Wall Tour will likely be his last, stating: "I'm not as young as I used to be. I'm not like B.B. King, or Muddy Waters. I'm not a great vocalist or a great instrumentalist or whatever, but I still have the fire in my belly, and I have something to say. I have a swan song in me and I think this will probably be it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">The O2 Arena</a> in London on 12 May 2011, Gilmour and Mason once again appeared with Waters and Gilmour performing "Comfortably Numb", and Gilmour and Mason joining Waters for "Outside the Wall".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> For the first half of 2012, Waters' tour topped worldwide concert ticket sales having sold more than 1.4 million tickets globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2013, The Wall Live is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">highest-grossing tour of all time by a solo artist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters performed at <a href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief" title="12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief">the Concert for Sandy Relief</a> at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> on 12 December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In 1969, Waters married his childhood sweetheart <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judy_Trim" title="Judy Trim">Judy Trim</a>, a successful potter; she was featured on the gatefold sleeve of the original release of <i><a href="/wiki/Ummagumma" title="Ummagumma">Ummagumma</a></i>, but excised from subsequent CD reissues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMabbett201050_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMabbett201050-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> They had no children together and divorced in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Trim died in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008376_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008376-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1976, Waters married <a href="/wiki/Carolyne_Christie" title="Carolyne Christie">Lady Carolyne Christie</a>, the niece of the <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Dundas,_3rd_Marquess_of_Zetland" title="Lawrence Dundas, 3rd Marquess of Zetland">3rd Marquess of Zetland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> His marriage to Christie produced a son, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Waters" title="Harry Waters">Harry Waters</a>, a musician who has played keyboards with his father's touring band since 2006, and a daughter, India Waters, who has worked as a model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Christie and Waters divorced in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005335-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1993, he married Priscilla Phillips; they had one son together, Jack Fletcher. Their marriage ended in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, he became engaged to actress and filmmaker Laurie Durning; the two married on 14 January 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activism">Activism</span></h2>
<p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_Earthquake" title="2004 Indian Ocean Earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean Earthquake</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> disaster, Waters performed "Wish You Were Here" with Eric Clapton during a benefit concert on the American network <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> He was outspoken against the <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act of 2004</a>, and performed a concert for, and attended marches supporting, the <a href="/wiki/Countryside_Alliance" title="Countryside Alliance">Countryside Alliance</a>. Waters explained:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I've become disenchanted with the political and philosophical atmosphere in England. The anti-hunting bill was enough for me to leave England. I did what I could, I did a concert and one or two articles, but it made me feel ashamed to be English. I was in Hyde Park for both the Countryside Alliance marches. There were hundreds of thousands of us there. Good, honest English people. That's one of the most divisive pieces of legislation we've ever had in Great Britain. It's not a case of whether or not I agree with fox hunting, but I will defend to the hilt their right to take part in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg"><img alt="In this scene, Waters punches the wall, while the projections simulate the wall crumbling as a result, revealing a bright sunset behind" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="668" data-file-width="1188" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg/280px-Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg/420px-Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg/560px-Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roger_Waters_The_Wall_Live_Kansas_City_30_October_2010_2.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Waters performing "Comfortably Numb" during The Wall Live in Kansas City, 30 October 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In October 2005, he clarified: "I come back to the UK quite often. I didn't leave as a protest against the hunting ban; I was following a child in the wake of a divorce."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> After leaving Britain, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> in New York with his fiancé Laurie Durning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391.E2.80.93392_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlake2008391.E2.80.93392-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2007, Waters became a spokesman for <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Promise" title="Millennium Promise">Millennium Promise</a>, a non-profit organisation that helps fight extreme poverty and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>. He wrote an opinion piece for <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> in support of the topic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> In July, he participated in the American leg of the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_New_York_City" title="Live Earth concert, New York City">Live Earth</a> concert, an international multi-venue concert aimed at raising awareness about global climate change, featuring the Trenton Youth Choir and his trademarked inflatable pig. Waters told <a href="/wiki/David_Fricke" title="David Fricke">David Fricke</a> why he thinks <i>The Wall</i> is still relevant today:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The loss of a father is the central prop on which [<i>The Wall</i>] stands. As the years go by, children lose their fathers again and again, for nothing. You see it now with all these fathers, good men and true, who lost their lives and limbs in Iraq for no reason at all. I've done Bring The Boys Back Home in my encore on recent tours. It feels more relevant and poignant to be singing that song now than it did in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFricke200974_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFricke200974-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 2012, Waters led a benefit for United States military veterans called Stand Up for Heroes. He invited a music group of combat wounded veterans called <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Bloom#MusiCorps" title="Arthur Bloom">MusiCorps</a> to perform with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2013, Waters and numerous other celebrities appeared in a video showing support for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradley_Manning" title="Bradley Manning">Bradley Manning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views">Political views</span></h2>
<p>Waters has been outspoken about Middle Eastern politics, and in June 2009 he opposed the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">Israeli West Bank barrier</a>, calling it an "obscenity [that] should be torn down".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, he pledged his support to the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Freedom_March" title="Gaza Freedom March">Gaza Freedom March</a>, and in 2011 he announced that he had joined the <a href="/wiki/Boycott,_Divestment_and_Sanctions" title="Boycott, Divestment and Sanctions">Boycott, Divestment and Sanctions</a> (BDS) movement against Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters spoke about his support for BDS, stating that he has "been very disillusioned with UK foreign policy ... since <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Wilson</a>. It was such a political turnabout from <a href="/wiki/Keir_Hardie" title="Keir Hardie">Keir Hardie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Attlee</a> and the principles of British socialism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2010, after an animated B52 bomber had been shown dropping symbols including the <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a> as part of The Wall Live tour, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League (ADL)</a> condemned Waters, saying that he had used "imagery long associated with steretotypes about Jews and money" and had "cross[ed] the line into anti-Semitism." In response, he wrote an open letter to <i>The Independent</i> in which he commented: "If I don't respond, people will see the story and will come to believe I'm anti-Semitic, and I'm not. Nothing could be further from the truth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP2010_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-JP2010-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> He explained that the artwork used during his shows is "representative of religious and national and commercial interests, all of which have a malign influence on our lives and prevent us from treating each other decently".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP2010_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-JP2010-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> He added: "You can attack Israeli policy without being anti-Jewish ... It's like saying if you criticise the US policy you are being anti-Christian. I'm critical of the Israeli policy of occupying Palestinian land and their policy of building settlements, which is entirely illegal under international law, and also of ghettoising the people whose land they are building on ... It's that foreign policy I'm against. It's nothing to do with the religion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP2010_116-2"><a href="#cite_note-JP2010-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2013, during an interview with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_Intifada" title="Electronic Intifada">Electronic Intifada</a></i>, Waters stated that the American media "was under instructions from somewhere not to report [criticism of Israel] to the American public, on what grounds I cannot guess."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 July 2013, during a concert in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Waters' road crew released a pig-shaped balloon that had been painted with symbols including a Star of David, other political symbols shown including representing fascist, communist and capitalist representations. As the balloon floated over the audience, Waters sang the lyrics to "In the Flesh": "get him up against the wall, that one looks Jewish and that one's a coon, who let all of this riff-raff into the room" while holding "a machine gun replica and wearing a long black leather jacket with a red-and-white arm band reminiscent of a Nazi uniform."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haaretz2013_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz2013-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JP2013_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-JP2013-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Rabbi Abraham Cooper, associate dean of the Simon Wiesenthal Center criticized him: "Waters deployed a classic disgusting medieval anti-Semitic caricature widely used by both Nazi and Soviet propaganda to incite hatred against Jews."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters responded to the accusations, characterizing Cooper's statement as "wild and bigoted" with an "entirely predictable resulting rant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSJ2013_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSJ2013-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters commented: "I should point out that in the show, I also use the Crucifix, the Crescent and Star, the Hammer and Sickle, the Shell Oil Logo and the McDonald’s Sign, a Dollar Sign and a Mercedes sign."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSJ2013_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSJ2013-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters explained that his father had died fighting Nazis and that he grew up in post-war England, receiving an in-depth education about the war: "I was spared no horrific detail of the heinous crimes committed in the name of that most foul ideology."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSJ2013_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-RSJ2013-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters stated that the Wall Show: "is many things. It is thoughtful, life affirming, ecumenical, humane, loving, anti-war, anti-colonial, pro-universal access to the law, pro-liberty, pro-collaboration, pro-dialogue, pro-peace, anti-authoritarian, anti-fascist, anti-apartheid, anti-dogma, international in spirit, musical and satirical. It is not anti-Semitic or pro-Nazi."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JB2013_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-JB2013-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters clarified his position regarding the use of religious imagery: "the Star of David represents Israel and its policies and is legitimately subject to any and all forms of non violent protest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSJ2013_121-3"><a href="#cite_note-RSJ2013-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters stated that the pig balloon represents "the evil of errant government."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSJ2013_121-4"><a href="#cite_note-RSJ2013-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> He added: "For the sake of some perspective. The inflatable pig ... has appeared at every Wall Show since September 2010, some 193 shows [and] yours is the first complaint."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JB2013_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-JB2013-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During a December 2013 interview in <i><a href="/wiki/CounterPunch" title="CounterPunch">CounterPunch</a></i> magazine, Waters made statements urging musicians to boycott Israel in response to their continued occupation of Palestine. He compared Israeli domestic policies with those of Nazi Germany, stating: "the parallels with what went on in the '30s in Germany are so crushingly obvious".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> In response, author Rabbi Shmuley Boteach accused Waters of anti-Semitism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters defended himself, pointing out that he was not criticising Jews or Israelis in general, but the actions of the Israeli state against the Palestinians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment_and_instruments">Equipment and instruments</span></h2>
<p>Waters' primary instrument in Pink Floyd was the electric bass guitar. He briefly played a <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6fner" title="Höfner">Höfner</a> bass but replaced it with a <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker" title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a> RM-1999/4001S, until 1970 when it was stolen along with the rest of the band's equipment in New Orleans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPovey200814_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPovey200814-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> He began using <a href="/wiki/Fender_Precision_Bass" title="Fender Precision Bass">Fender Precision Basses</a> in 1968, originally alongside the Rickenbacker, and then exclusively after the Rickenbacker was lost in 1970. First seen at a concert in Hyde Park, London in July 1970, the black P-Bass was rarely used until April 1972 when it became his main stage guitar and as of 2 October 2010, the basis for a Fender Artist Signature model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters endorses <a href="/wiki/RotoSound" title="RotoSound">RotoSound</a> Jazz Bass 77 flat-wound strings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout his career he has used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Selmer_Company" title="The Selmer Company">Selmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Electric_Music" title="Watkins Electric Music">WEM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiwatt" title="Hiwatt">Hiwatt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashdown_Engineering" title="Ashdown Engineering">Ashdown</a> amplifiers but has used <a href="/wiki/Ampeg" title="Ampeg">Ampeg</a> for the last few tours, also employing <a href="/wiki/Delay_(audio_effect)" title="Delay (audio effect)">delay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tremolo" title="Tremolo">tremolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chorus_effect" title="Chorus effect">chorus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stereo_panning" title="Stereo panning">stereo panning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phaser_(effect)" title="Phaser (effect)">phaser</a> effects in his bass playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005416.E2.80.93430.2C_441.E2.80.93445_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005416.E2.80.93430.2C_441.E2.80.93445-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Waters experimented with the <a href="/wiki/EMS_Synthi_A" title="EMS Synthi A">EMS Synthi A</a> and <a href="/wiki/EMS_VCS_3" title="EMS VCS 3">VCS 3</a> synthesisers on Pink Floyd pieces such as "<a href="/wiki/On_the_Run_(instrumental)" title="On the Run (instrumental)">On the Run</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMason2005169_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMason2005169-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Machine" title="Welcome to the Machine">Welcome to the Machine</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005324_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005324-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Flesh%3F" title="In the Flesh?">In the Flesh?</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitchMahon200671_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitchMahon200671-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> He played electric and acoustic guitar on Pink Floyd tracks using Fender, Martin, <a href="/wiki/Ovation_Guitar_Company" title="Ovation Guitar Company">Ovation</a> and Washburn guitars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005416.E2.80.93430.2C_441.E2.80.93445_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005416.E2.80.93430.2C_441.E2.80.93445-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> He played electric guitar on the Pink Floyd song "<a href="/wiki/Sheep_(song)" title="Sheep (song)">Sheep</a>", from <i>Animals</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005285_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005285-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> and acoustic guitar on several Pink Floyd recordings, such as <a href="/wiki/Pigs_on_the_Wing" title="Pigs on the Wing">"Pigs on the Wing 1 &amp; 2"</a>, also from <i>Animals</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005241.E2.80.93242_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005241.E2.80.93242-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Southampton_Dock" title="Southampton Dock">Southampton Dock</a>" from <i>The Final Cut</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005295_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005295-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> and on "<a href="/wiki/Mother_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Mother (Pink Floyd song)">Mother</a>" from <i>The Wall</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005213_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005213-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> A Binson Echorec 2 echo effect was used on his bass-guitar lead track "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_of_These_Days_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="One of These Days (Pink Floyd song)">One of These Days</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMabbett199539_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMabbett199539-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Waters plays clarinet during concert performances of "<a href="/wiki/Outside_the_Wall" title="Outside the Wall">Outside the Wall</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2005232_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2005232-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
